Xu Xinwu and Others Arrive in Jinan to Discuss Flood Barrier Project

Mei Yilin Goes to Western Shandong to Inspect River Works

(Jinan) Xu Xinwu and engineers Wang Fengxi and Lu Keming arrived in Jinan to meet with Han and discuss the flood barrier. Xu said that the Yellow River management work includes: (A) The flood barrier project, of which Hebei bears the greatest burden and the greatest harm affects Shandong; (B) Repairing the dikes. The section near the East Dam of Lanfeng and the west side of the Pinghan Railway Bridge is the most critical. If the East Dam is not repaired, a breach will turn Western Shandong and Northern Jiangsu into a swamp. If the section west of the Pinghan Bridge breaches, the Xiangwei River may flow from Hebei into the sea, causing great harm to North China. Both are matters of national concern, not just a portion. There are still many other dangerous works that should be repaired. (C) Raising and thickening the dikes along the entire river. This committee is only planning whether it can be implemented, depending on the central government's financial resources. Before leaving, I met with Wang, who said that 500,000 yuan would be allocated first to deal with the first step of the flood barrier project, with subsequent allocations later. The first zone is Henan, with engineer Cai Lianggong; the second zone is Hebei, with engineer Wang Fengxi; the third zone is Shandong, with engineer Lu Keming. But it is not strictly divided, and cooperation will occur when needed. The Yellow River Committee and the provincial governments will also cooperate as a principle. The breaches are in Zhengzhou, Lanfeng, Kaocheng, and Wenxian in Henan, and Erfenzhuang and Shitouzhuan in Hebei, of which Shitouzhuan has as many as 32 breaches. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee has transferred Mei Yilin, a section chief of the Military Affairs Commission, to Western Shandong to inspect the flood and river works. The provincial government has sent Xin Zhujiu from the Relief Committee to accompany him. Mei and Xin are scheduled to meet in Jizhou on the 7th and go to Caozhou together. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) The Western Shandong Flood Relief Emergency Committee has hired Ma Lianliang to perform in a play for three days to raise funds for disaster relief. Ticket prices are divided into four types: 4 yuan, 2 yuan, 1 yuan, and 5 jiao [half a yuan], which can raise more than 50,000 yuan. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Today the middle reaches of the Luokou rose by 8 centimeters, with a water level of 30 meters, 1 cun [Chinese inch], and 7 fen [Chinese tenth of a cun]. The upper reaches are falling, and the lower reaches have level water. The canal in Northern Shandong is also stopping water. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Xu Xinwu and others met with Han to describe the projects in the three zones. To block the breach in Erfenzhuang on the south bank, the central government will provide funds, and Shandong will provide labor, transferring personnel from the River Bureau to work. Han greatly approved, arguing that the faster the better. He immediately ordered Zhang Lianjia, Director of the River Bureau, to discuss with Xu and others in detail. The engineering office can be established within three to five days. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

American Embassy Female Secretary Assaulted by Japanese Troops

Intervention by the French Military Attache Ends It

(Beiping) Ms. Agelow, the personal secretary of American Minister to China Johnson, was riding a horse around the area of Jiaomin Lane yesterday when she was savagely attacked by armed soldiers of the Japanese Embassy guard. All foreign circles in Beiping are very resentful about this matter. The Japanese military did not notify other embassies in advance, nor did they post signs along the road. Suddenly, during exercises, they forbade riders from passing through the sections they occupied, only giving riders unnamed notes written in pencil. Ms. Agelow disregarded it and continued forward. Upon her return, more than ten Japanese soldiers surrounded her with bayonets fixed. One of them threw a large rock at Ms. Agelow's horse, and others struck Ms. Agelow's arm and broke her riding crop. Several soldiers even grabbed the horse's reins and tried to forcibly take Ms. Agelow away. Later, the commander of the French Embassy guard witnessed this and intervened, preventing her from further suffering violence. (5th Day North China Daily News Telegram)

Yu Xuezhong Returns to Tianjin

(Tianjin) Hebei Chairman Yu Xuezhong arrived in Tianjin by special train from Beijing at noon on the 6th, carrying his entourage and guards. Leaders of provincial and municipal agencies all came to the station to welcome him. After getting off the train, Yu went directly to the provincial government and then met with reporters in the reception hall. According to him, he had traveled south for about a month, visiting Chairman Chiang in Lushan about five or six times, and reported on the military and political affairs of Hebei Province. On foreign affairs issues, he adopted a consistent approach with the Political Affairs Committee. After the military affairs are over, the original organization will be restored. Regarding financial matters, Chiang agreed to find ways to help. In Beijing, he met with President Wang and Minister Song one after another. On financial matters, he expressed the same thing as Chiang. He hoped to restore the original 4.5 million yuan status as soon as possible before the war. After resting, he will go to Beiping to visit He. Regarding the bandit suppression in LuanDong, he will deliberate carefully. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Sui Province Requests Allocation of Relief Funds

(Nanjing) Sui Province Chairman Fu Zuoyi telegraphed Wang and Song, stating that because the province was affected by Yellow River flooding, the area flooded is over 300 square li [Chinese mile], with 200,000 displaced people. He requested an allocation of funds for relief. The Yellow River Conservancy Commission immediately replied by telegram, saying that in addition to requesting the Flood Relief Committee to allocate relief funds, they also hoped to send staff and conscript laborers to work together to prevent the disaster area from expanding. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Funds Have Not Yet Been Allocated

(Nanjing) After the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee is formed, it will hold a formal meeting as soon as Commissioner Song returns to Beijing from Lushan to discuss relief policies. Although the funds for Yellow River disaster relief have been set at 4 million yuan, they have not yet been allocated. Whether they will be allocated from the American cotton and wheat loan will be decided after Song returns to Beijing. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Fujian Fellow Provincials in Beijing Request Allocation of Cotton and Wheat Loan

(Nanjing) The Fujian Fellow Provincials Association in Beijing submitted a petition to the National Government, stating that Fujian Province has suffered frequent floods and droughts in recent years, and communist bandits have ravaged the area, causing farmers to be destitute and homeless. The $50 million American cotton and wheat loan is intended for construction and rural reconstruction. The disaster in Fujian is the most severe, and rural reconstruction is particularly urgent. They earnestly requested the Executive Yuan to allocate a larger portion of the cotton and wheat loan than other provinces in the overall distribution and to select honest and capable commissioners to be responsible for planning and construction and rural reconstruction. (6th Day Telegram)

Li Yizhi Prepares to Depart for Three-Province Inspection

(Nanjing) Yellow River Conservancy Commission Director Li Yizhi is scheduled to depart on the 8th for the three provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan to inspect the construction status of the downstream Yellow River flood prevention project. He is scheduled to go to Jinan first to meet with Xu Xinwu and inspect Shandong and Hebei, then go to Lanfeng and Xi'an to start planning fundamental river management methods. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Chiang Convenes Meeting on Relief of Grain and Rice

Scheduled to Open on the 21st

(Nanchang) Because the low price of grain harms farmers and a crisis is looming, Chairman Chiang telegraphed representatives from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Guangdong, and Shanghai to arrive in Jiangxi before the 20th to hold a meeting on relief of grain and rice. The main points are: (1) To connect rice-producing areas with rice-deficient areas and prevent foreign rice from invading the interior; (2) To store grain for famine preparedness; (3) To request an allocation of American wheat and to establish new granaries in various places to mortgage grain and circulate rural finance. The plan will be assisted by the agricultural banks of four provinces, and the meeting is scheduled to open on the 21st. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Dike Breached in Lijin

More Than Forty Villages Flooded

(Jinan) The civil dike on the north bank of the Yellow River downstream at the estuary in Lijin breached, flooding over forty villages, including Xinzhuozhuang, turning them into a swamp. Representatives, including Yue Dingfu, have been sent to Jinan to request emergency relief to block the breach. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Belgian Minister Passes Through Beijing to Shanghai

(Nanjing) Belgian Minister de Groote and his family arrived in Beijing from Beiping on the afternoon of the 6th and left for Shanghai at 5:30. His mission is to inspect the affairs of the various consulates and will stay in Shanghai for two months before returning north. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Banks in Beiping Continue to Discuss Ways to Prevent Bandits

Additional Petitioner Police Assigned in Front of Each Bank

(Beiping) The banks in Beiping convened a full committee meeting at the Bankers' Association this afternoon to discuss ways to prevent bandits. It was resolved to request the Municipal Public Security Bureau to assign additional petitioner police in front of each bank and office for defense. Wang Shaoxian and Wang Zemin were designated to go to the Public Security Bureau tomorrow to negotiate the additional allocation. (6th Day Special Dispatch)

Use of Dutch庚子 Indemnity Funds

A portion to be used for water conservancy, a portion for scholarships.

Singapore: According to Mr. Song Faxiang, Consul-General stationed in Batavia, Dutch庚子 Indemnity funds will be allocated to subsidize Chinese students who graduate from Dutch schools in Java and Sumatra. Chinese students who have already graduated in Java will be sent back to China to specialize in Chinese language studies. Then, the government will send them to various universities in the Netherlands at public expense. This project has been approved by the Dutch government. The Dutch庚子 Indemnity will be fully returned to China starting in 1926. Sixty-five percent of these funds will be used to manage the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, to reduce the risk of flooding from the two rivers. The remaining thirty-five percent will be designated as scholarships for sending Chinese students to the Netherlands. To provide Javanese Chinese students with scholarship opportunities, the Netherlands will revise the curriculum of Chinese schools, as Chinese schools only focus on English and Chinese. Mr. Song intends to suggest that Chinese students at the Batavia Medical College and the Padang Institute of Technology should have the opportunity to obtain scholarships. However, those going to the Netherlands must study Chinese for at least two years. (Reuter's dispatch, 6th)

Reasons for Rejection by the Central Political Council of the Customs' Request for Additional Budget

(Nanjing) The Customs has recently suffered losses of over 600,000 taels per month due to the impact of gold prices. The Ministry of Finance submitted a request for an additional budget, which was rejected by the Central Political Council on August 23. The reasons given were: Since there are times when gold and silver exchange rates are lower than income, there should also be times when they are higher. With multiple exchanges, the highs and lows should offset each other. Even if the result is a profit or loss, it should not be excessively loss-making. The total number of gold units sold this year is 52 million, and the exchange loss between China and the United States has reached more than 3 million. For two months, the losses have almost exceeded the profits. If there is any dishonesty or incompleteness in the process, it would be tantamount to willingly accepting exploitation and deception from financial institutions, and the blame for poor management would be unavoidable. The national treasury can hardly bear such improper losses. Moreover, after the budget is announced, the restrictions on submitting additional requests are extremely strict. It is only stipulated that additional requests can be made when there are unavoidable situations under the law or contract where there is a shortfall. The conditions of this case do not meet these criteria. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Ministry of Communications Stipulates Swimming Examination Measures for Seafarers

(Nanjing) In order to cope with the dangers of navigation on rivers and seas, the Ministry of Communications has stipulated four measures for the swimming examination of senior seafarers: ㈠ Seafarers' swimming examinations will be held simultaneously with the certification process. ㈡ Vocational schools for merchant shipping may hold examinations at the school. Students who fail the swimming test will not be allowed to graduate. ㈢ Seafarers must swim at least 100 yards freestyle in calm waters to pass. ㈣ The Ministry will not issue seafarer certificates to those who fail the swimming test. The above items will be implemented from January 1 next year. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Two Cases of Government Officials Impeached for Neglect of Duty and Malfeasance

(Nanjing) Supervisory Committee member Zhou Lisheng of the Control Yuan impeached Wu Han, the Shandong Luda Coal Tax Commissioner, for corruption and neglect of duty. Supervisory Committee member Shao Hongji impeached Wu Bingyan, an official of the Jiangsu Anhui Liansi Donggan Shuyan Liquor License Tax Collection Bureau, for illegal malfeasance. The Central Government Officials Punishment Committee has decided that Wu Han should be handed over to the competent court for handling in accordance with the law, and the matter will be reviewed after the criminal proceedings are concluded. Wu Bingyan's monthly salary will be reduced by 10% for a period of three months. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Central Organization Committee Sends Personnel to Study Local Autonomy

(Nanjing) The Central Organization Committee will select five party members in each county to specialize in the study of local autonomy, cooperative undertakings, Baojia movement, social education, and rural economy issues. After two months, the central government will send personnel to assess them. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Chiang Kai-shek Transfers Army University Students to Jiangxi

(Nanjing) Chiang Kai-shek telegraphed the General Staff Headquarters, ordering the transfer of graduates from the eighth, ninth, and special classes of the Army University to Jiangxi, to await assignment. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Overseas Delegates to the Fifth National Congress Arrive in Shaanxi for Inspection

(Nanjing) The delegation of overseas delegates to the Fifth National Congress arrived in the province at 4 p.m. on the 5th and stayed at the Xi'an Hotel. At 7 p.m., Shao Lizi hosted a banquet at the Provincial Government, accompanied by Zhang Zhijun of the Provincial Guidance Committee and others. According to Huang Hunxing of the delegation, who spoke to a Central News Agency reporter, the members of this trip are Ren Chaohai, Executive Committee member of the Branch in Borneo, Fang Guoji, representative in India, Meng Yu, Liu Yeqing, Huang Hunxing, He Linxi, the four representatives in Cuba, Guo Hanjie, the representative in Annam, Liang Shijun, Chen Jixu, Li Xianqing, the three representatives in Siam, totaling ten people. Because the Fifth National Congress has been postponed, they are taking the opportunity to come to the Northwest to investigate industry and agriculture, so that they can promote the situation in the Northwest to overseas Chinese in the future. The central government has sent two cadres to take care of them along the way. They originally planned to go to Gansu, Ningxia, and Qinghai provinces, but will now decide based on transportation conditions. They plan to stay in Shaanxi for ten days. After the inspection is completed, they will go north to inspect the war zone and then south to inspect the bandit areas, and return to Nanjing before the opening of the Fifth National Congress. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Shaanxi Province Exempts Disaster Areas from Land Tax

(Nanjing) The Provincial Government previously consulted the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Interior to exempt the disaster areas in the province from land tax. This has been approved by the Executive Yuan meeting. The land tax owed by the people in the seriously affected counties of the western route for the 19th and 20th years will be completely exempted, and the tax owed for the 21st year will be deferred. This has also been approved by the National Government for record. The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Finance have replied to the Provincial Government, ordering the Finance Department to comply on the 5th. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Wang Yongbin Cables Nanjing to Continue His Leave

(Nanjing) Wang Yongbin, Chairman of the Examination Committee, was summoned by Chiang Kai-shek to Lushan. As the matter has not yet been completed, he cabled Nanjing to continue his leave for five days, and will return to Nanjing around the 10th to preside over the second session of the Higher Civil Service Examination. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Ministry of Communications Abolishes Wireless Telegraph Secret Code News Regulations

(Nanjing) On the 6th, the Ministry of Communications issued an order to abolish the Provisional Regulations on the Transmission of News Telegrams in Secret Code by Radio Stations, promulgated in June of the 18th year of the Republic. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Shanghai-Pingjin Joint Transportation Collects Cash Only

(Nanjing) As the Shanghai-Pingjin through train service has started ahead of the Pingpu and Jinghu lines, the Railway Ministry has ordered that all purchase freight and transportation fees must be collected in cash. All preferential certificates and registered travel are strictly prohibited, and will not be applicable. The matter has been approved by the National Government. The order has been telegraphed to the Jinghu, Huhangyong, Jinpu, and Beining Railway Bureaus for compliance. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Mongolian League Urges Establishment of Radio Stations

(Nanjing) On the 6th, the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission sent another letter to the Ministry of Communications, stating that with national defense as the priority, wireless radio stations should be rapidly built in Chahar, Suiyuan, Kangding, and Dihua, so that communication with the central government will not be interrupted. (Special Dispatch, 6th)

Current Commentary

The Self-Awareness of Responsibility in Naval Circles

Since Xie Gangzhe took office as commander of the Third Fleet of the Navy, he has moved the headquarters and training team to Weihaiwei. Although other affiliated units still remain in Qingdao, they are also ordered to move outside the city. According to Xie, the motivation for this move is, first, to avoid the suspicion of interfering in politics, and second, to get rid of the atmosphere of extravagance. Well said! How pleasant it is to hear! Military arrogance has been around for a long time. Indolence has become a habit, and it is difficult to change. The reason why the country has declined to this point is that these people should bear the majority of the responsibility. We are extremely heartbroken, but we have never made a clear indication. How fortunate it is that Xie has issued this edict, and how fortunate it is to hear the words of self-awareness of responsibility from the mouth of a military leader!

Originally, it is the duty of soldiers to defend the country, and they should not engage in political activities. It is the urgent task of soldiers to forge their skills, and how can they allow themselves to be contaminated with decadent habits? However, today, many soldiers in our country regard military service as a special class, and rely on it as a shortcut to advancement. They have no thought of defending the country in their hearts, let alone the intention of striving for strength. From superiors to soldiers, almost all harbor a leisurely goal, and seek to achieve it deviously. Because they take enjoyment as their purpose, they try every means to interfere in politics to help their development. Also, because they have gained the opportunity to interfere in politics, they further increase their desire for extravagance. Such mutual causation and mutual push will make it impossible to prevent the corruption of military discipline.

The impact of military interference in politics often unsettles the political world and adds many unnecessary disturbances. The result of military enjoyment must reduce the ambition to fight and lose the cultivation of skills. This is a particularly common phenomenon in our naval circles. The navy is merely a formality, with few achievements, and often engages in instigating chaos and aiding disasters during turbulent political situations. We have already presented our accusations in the past. Recently, the test firing of a warship in Chu actually resulted in the rebound of a shell. Even after a new repair, with full preparation, in a public test, and under careful supervision, there was still this unexpected accident. Then, how is the usual combat exercise? How is the cultivation of skills? It is unimaginable. Supervisory Committee member Gao Youtang said that the navy has no reputation to speak of. Even we feel that his words are too harsh. Can the officers and soldiers of the navy endure this with shame forever? Or will they be determined to work hard and try to wash away this disgrace?

To wash away disgrace does not lie in retorting, but in self-reflection without guilt. The way to wash away disgrace cannot be borrowed from empty words as a tool for concealment, but must be based on facts as the final proof. For example, Navy Commander Chen Shaokuan said that the rebounding of shells is not surprising. This kind of excuse is not what we like to hear. It is necessary for Xie Gangzhe to have a self-aware expression before we can expect it. Since Xie has already spoken out first, he should be able to restrain himself afterwards. We hope that Xie will, from now on, sharpen his mind and strength, calmly go to the opportunity, and thoroughly clarify his true self-awareness of responsibility. We also hope that all the officers and soldiers of the navy will, under this encouragement and urging, understand that it is not convenient to hold a position without doing any work for a long time, and that it is no longer possible to steal a moment of peace. They should beat their chests and pull out their hair, and rise up together to jointly seek the self-awareness of responsibility of the entire navy. Then, the destruction of seeking perfection can be avoided, and unexpected praise can be achieved. We express our infinite hope for the development of a new atmosphere in the navy.

Success of Cuban Revolution, Provisional Government Established

Chairman of the Provisional Government, Portela, concurrently serves as Minister of Foreign Affairs, the new government denies any communist tendencies, American warships arrive in Cuba to protect overseas Chinese

Havana: The Cespedes government of Cuba has been overthrown again. Revolutionary soldiers have united with radical opposition parties to form a revolutionary committee, and Professor Grau of San Martin University has been elected as the leader to temporarily govern. (National Telegram, 5th)

Havana: The Cuban Revolutionary Committee has assigned the various departments of the new government to the five executive committee members. Chairman Portela concurrently holds the positions of Minister of Justice and Minister of Foreign Affairs. Carbo holds the positions of Minister of Interior, Minister of Transportation, Minister of Army, and Minister of Navy. Franga serves as Minister of Finance. Samartan serves as Minister of Education and Minister of Health. Irizali serves as Minister of Public Works, Minister of Agriculture, and Minister of Commerce. The deputy ministers of the respective departments will remain in their original positions. (Havas Dispatch, 6th)

Havana: While the newly appointed Cuban President Cespedes was out of the capital investigating the wind disaster, Sergeant Batista of the army, in conjunction with a university professor and a radical journalist, ousted Cespedes and organized what they called a "Genuine Revolutionary Government." Batista claimed that the army and navy supported him, and stated that his purpose was to purge the officers who supported former President Machado and to revive Cuba according to the latest concept of democracy. Gunfire has been frequent in the city today, but all shots have been fired into the air and no casualties have been reported. Batista immediately announced that he was prepared to hand over power to a legally elected congress, and that Cuba's treaty obligations would be respected. An orderly demonstration is currently taking place in the streets, and troops are patrolling the streets to prevent accidents. President Cespedes rushed back to the capital upon hearing the news, but the Minister of Interior has announced that he and the former cabinet members are prepared to cooperate with the new government. (Reuter's Dispatch, 5th)

Beginning of the Revolution

According to reports, when yesterday's incident first began, it was nothing more than a military mutiny. Officers who clung to former President Machado were expelled and detained. Staff Sergeant Gang Chailai was publicly elected as Chief of Staff. Gang esteemed Staff Sergeant Batista as superior to him. Therefore, these two staff sergeants became the commanders of the entire army and formed a temporary dictatorship. The police also joined the revolution.

Formation of the Government

Later, the radical opposition party, which claimed to be liberal, and the military that began to transform the mutiny into a political revolution. Gang and Ba knew that they had no political experience, so they followed their advice and organized a revolutionary committee with five members, electing Professor Grau as the leader, and Lieutenant Delatour as the capable person and spokesperson.

Forcing the President to Leave

After the Revolutionary Committee was established, it immediately demanded that President Cespedes reform politics. The President agreed. Then, they demanded that the cabinet resign. When the cabinet resigned en masse, they were still dissatisfied. A few hours later, they requested that the President cede his position. Cespedes left the Presidential Palace immediately, but stated that he had not yet resigned because there was no suitable authority to accept his resignation. Thus, the Revolutionary Committee moved into the Presidential Palace to work.

Organization of the Five-Member Executive Committee

Havana: The Cuban Revolutionary Committee has recently appointed five executive committee members: ㈠ Dr. Samartan, ㈡ Dr. Portela, ㈢ Dr. Irizali, ㈣ Carbo, ㈤ Franga. Army Sergeant Batista, originally from Chile and later naturalized as a Cuban, who advocated for the revolution, is now being promoted to Commander-in-Chief of the Army. Some parties have expressed concern about the organization of the executive committee, with some people leaning towards extremism, especially Carbo, who is a writer who has lived in the Soviet Union for two years. The five executive committee members mentioned above have equal power, and Portela only nominally holds the position of Executive Chairman. The current head of the National Police Department has been dismissed and replaced by Sergeant Laurent. The position of Chief of Staff of the Navy has also been assumed by another sergeant. (Havas Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Issuance of Public Announcements

After the committee forced the president to leave, it issued several public announcements to declare its plans and policies. One stated that it would respect national debts, especially foreign debts. Another denied any intention to greatly change the government system, saying it would organize a provisional government, convene a constitutional conference, and amend the constitution. A third announced that several officers who had been clinging to Machado had been dismissed after military trials, but denied reports of officers being shot in Havana. According to Lieutenant Delatour, the spokesperson for the committee, the Cespedes government could not represent the people and should be greatly reformed. The public announcement also stated that the committee did not want to hold power for long, and would resign as soon as the constitutional currency, economy, and military reforms were guaranteed. Delatour also stated that there was absolutely no resentment towards the arrival of American warships here.

Party Support

Havana: The ABC party, which was in a leading position when the Machado government was overthrown, announced today after a lengthy meeting that it would maintain a neutral position towards the new government. This declaration is expected to benefit the new government and greatly increase its chances of establishing a solid foundation. (National News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Denial of Leaning to the Left

Professor Grau is a professor at San Martin University and a famous revolutionary figure, but his attitude is more appropriately described as liberal than radical. So far, there is no communist color among the revolutionary leaders. Grau also stated that he would not allow such radical figures to participate in the new revolution. However, there are some parties who are quite apprehensive about the deterioration of the situation, or leading to the participation of communists.

Batista's Brief History

Havana: The experience of Sergeant Batista, the leader of the army and navy rebellion in Cuba, is roughly as follows: Before joining the army, Batista was a stenographer who served in the judicial system, achieving the best results. For the past eight years, he has been responsible for the records of military courts. Taking this opportunity, he became acquainted with a majority of university students and figures of the Machado opposition party. It is rumored outside that this rebellion was due to the government's plan to cut military pay, but Batista denied this. It is also said that Batista personally has a relationship with the Machado faction, which he also denied. Former Army Chief Herrera declared that he did not know such a person. Batista said that the soldiers and junior officers who seized command this time are prepared to return to their original ranks as soon as the government is organized, and will still obey officers who have not harmed the people. Batista also said that there is absolutely no communist movement in the army and navy, and he would never tolerate it if there was one. (Havas Dispatch, 5th)

Business as Usual

The capital is currently as peaceful as usual. The people regard the revolution as no different from an election. The armies of the outer provinces have not yet expressed opposition to the revolutionary leaders here. However, the situation is still uncertain, because there seems to be a lack of central power to guarantee order. The Revolutionary Committee has only gained the support of several sergeants who claim to represent the army and navy. President Cespedes has not formally resigned, and his cabinet members are actually standing aside and doing nothing.

Shooting of Officers

There has been news that several military leaders who held military power during the Machado era have been shot in the camps. It is also heard that the authorities have drafted a list of those who should be shot, with quite a number of people listed. Four officers were also shot by soldiers in the Santiago area.

Anti-American Actions

It is also heard that radical elements have asked the committee to eliminate American influence. According to a gentleman from the American Legion, this news is quite certain, and the lives of American nationals are in danger. He and another veteran walked all over Havana tonight to notify American and other foreign nationals that if they saw any signs of anti-foreign riots, they should immediately take refuge in the National Hotel. The veterans will cooperate with the US Marines to take responsibility for protection.

US Sends Warships

The US destroyer McFarland has arrived here from Key West. Four more are on the way. Although US Ambassador Wells has indirectly warned all factions that if a civil war occurs, it will inevitably lead to intervention, he still represents US Secretary of State Hull in declaring that this dispatch of warships has no intention of interfering, but is only to protect the lives of American nationals. Seeing this situation, the leaders of the various factions have rushed to the US Embassy to guarantee that there will be no bloodshed.

Intervention Threat

US Ambassador Wells is currently busy consulting with the revolutionary leaders on everything and reporting the situation to Washington. Although he has not openly threatened to intervene, he has indirectly warned the Revolutionary Committee and Lieutenant Delatour that if an open rebellion occurs, the US Marines will land immediately. However, the embassy has stated that whether or not it intervenes, it will not endanger Cuba's independence. (National Telegram, 5th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull and Mr. Reiff, the State Department's specialist in Latin American affairs (who will succeed Welles as Ambassador to Cuba), visited President Roosevelt to discuss the Cuban situation for a long time. They also discussed the possibility of American intervention. After the meeting, a public announcement was made stating that in addition to the several warships already sent to Cuba, more will be sent to park in the vicinity of Cuban waters. Looking at the current situation, if a civil war breaks out in Cuba, the United States will definitely act quickly, but senior State Department officials say that there has been no decision on this matter, and they do not approve of any action by the United States. President Roosevelt said that the United States had not interfered and was able to make Machado resign, and its prestige could be said to be very strong. He does not want to lose this hard-earned prestige, but some people speculate that the United States may be in a situation where it cannot help but intervene. In addition, the acting president of Cuba, Cespedes, is only sheltering in a private residence, and has not actually formally resigned. The newly appointed US Ambassador to Cuba, Mr. Caffery, declared, "Our country certainly has the power to intervene according to the Platt Amendment, but the United States is extremely averse to actually exercising this power." He also said that what the United States government values most is maintaining friendly relations with neighboring countries in international affairs. (Havas Dispatch, 5th)

Chen Ce Visits French Naval Facilities

Marseilles: Chen Ce, former commander of the Guangdong Navy in China, and his party, who have been inspecting the French Third Naval District for the past few days, arrived at the Berre Lake naval base by plane from Toulon today to visit various facilities and affairs. Rear Admiral de Barra, the acting port commander, and Lieutenant Colonel Doma, commander of the Berre Lake naval base, accompanied Chen Ce and others as guides. (Havas Dispatch, 5th)

British Fleet to Visit Japan, Yokohama Prepares to Welcome

Yokohama: The British Far East Fleet will visit Japan in the near future. Preparations are currently underway here to welcome them. The entire fleet will be divided into several groups, visiting various ports in Japan from September 28 to October 27. Its Commander-in-Chief, Vice Admiral Dreyer, will travel to Yokohama and other places on the flagship Kent. (Reuter's Dispatch, 6th)

Japan Plans Countermeasures for the Next Washington Conference

Three Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy Form Committee

(Tokyo) Britain and the United States intend to take advantage of the Second Washington Naval Disarmament Conference in 1935 to restrain Japan's power in the Pacific. On the Japanese side, the effect of withdrawing from the League of Nations will also occur at the same time as the Washington Conference in 1935, and Japan's international position will be extremely unfavorable. Encountering a truly major situation, it is necessary for the three ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, and Navy, as well as the General Staff Headquarters and the Naval General Staff Department, to have full and close communication. It has been decided to organize a permanent liaison committee within the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the first meeting will be held at noon on the 7th. (Den Tsū Telegraph, 6th)

Contents of the Draft Investigation Department of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs

Exerting the Skills of Economic Diplomacy, Specialized Investigation of Reddening of China and Japan

Tokyo News: The draft of the Investigation Department of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs was suspended due to the incompatibility between the original plan during Yoshizawa's tenure and the nature of the diplomatic policy decision-making body like the Diplomatic Investigation Council advocated by the Privy Council. Afterwards, several new plans were drafted, and negotiations were conducted with the Privy Council. Recently, Vice Minister Shigemitsu visited each advisor of the Privy Council and obtained their understanding. As a result, the final draft of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was prepared, and the Director General of the Legislation Bureau, Kurosaki, requested the Privy Council Examination Committee to review it. The contents of the final draft of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which will be discussed in September, are as follows: ㈠ An investigation department will be established within the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to participate in the investigation and planning of various diplomatic affairs. It is necessary to ensure that the department only has the nature of an administrative bureau and has no diplomatic decision-making power. ㈡ The head of the department will be a Choku-nin official. ㈢ The department will be divided into five sections: the first section will investigate the diplomatic situation in Asia, the second section will investigate the diplomatic situation in Europe and the United States, the third section will specifically investigate the reddening propaganda of China, Manchuria, and Japan, the fourth section will investigate the trade and economic situation of various countries, and the fifth section will be responsible for liaison with other sections and accounting affairs. The special establishment of a section for investigating reddening propaganda is due to considering the ideological problems within Japan, the activities of the Chinese Communist Party, the Russian propaganda along the Chinese Eastern Railway, and the active progress of Soviet Russia in Xinjiang Province, China. The section was established after considering the opinions of the Privy Council, to exert the skills of trade investigation and economic diplomacy. The Trade Deliberation Council, which is scheduled to be held in September, will only meet for one or two days, but the council has a permanent nature and will be held at any time when necessary in the future. The Investigation Department has an administrative nature, while the council has the nature of an advisory council. (World News Agency)

The Japanese Military Decides to Reform Military System

Adopting the Latest Weaponry to Increase Combat Power, Transferring Five Divisions to the Korean-Manchurian Border to Prepare for Russia

(Tokyo) The Japanese Army Ministry has decided to reform the military system starting next spring. According to the Japanese military, the proposal for military system reform was delayed due to the busy response to the September 18th Incident, which prevented internal reforms. Now that the Manchurian incident has come to an end, they can focus all their efforts on internal reforms. The main points of the proposed reform plan are as follows: 1) Five standing army divisions will be transferred to the Manchurian and Korean borders with Russia to counter the Soviet Union. This requires revising matters related to the garrison locations, troop strength, and organization of the standing army in the country. 2) Each army will be equipped with various new types of military machinery and ammunition, emphasizing scientific roles and supplementing combat power. (Sixth Day Chinese United Press Dispatch)

Japan's Latent Crisis

Facing Internal and External Difficulties, Industrial Recovery Ultimately Becomes a Fantasy

| Commentary from Russian Newspaper |

(Moscow) The Soviet government gazette "Izvestia" published an editorial analyzing Japan's domestic situation. The newspaper, in commenting on the recent cabinet reshuffle movement in Japan, pointed out that the essence of Prime Minister Saito's political strategy is to paralyze the efforts of the Seiyukai to undermine the cabinet. After detailing the economic situation in Japan, the newspaper concluded that the economic panic continues to deepen and intensify, while the so-called industrial recovery is merely a fantasy. The current financial situation constitutes the most serious problem for Japanese capitalists, and the most difficult problem is how to find funds to continue their insane arms expansion. In addition to these problems, the increasingly complex and tense international situation further exacerbates the situation. Thus, Japanese imperialism is facing the greatest difficulties, while the domestic political situation is becoming increasingly tense, and the people's dissatisfaction is growing daily. Even the panic of the police has failed to curb the growth of "dangerous thoughts." "Izvestia" concludes that this situation has promoted the attempt of various opposing political parties belonging to the same class to unite and cooperate. (Fifth Day TASS Dispatch)

Japanese Prime Minister Receives Representatives of the House of Peers

Seeking Understanding Through Compromise with Political Parties

(Tokyo) Japanese Prime Minister Saito Makoto received representatives of various factions of the House of Peers at 4:00 PM today. More than forty people attended. Speaker Konoe did not attend due to illness. Saito explained the meeting with the presidents of the three parties in the House of Representatives and requested spiritual assistance from the various factions in the House of Peers. Duke Ichijo questioned the Prime Minister, saying that after the public trial of the May 15th Incident, the people's resentment towards political parties has deepened. Is the government compromising with political parties? Saito replied that the government is only seeking spiritual assistance from the various factions in the House of Representatives and has not coordinated national policies, so there is no question of compromise or non-compromise. Due to the serious domestic and foreign situation, he requested that the spirit of both houses be united to support the government and overcome this crisis. (Sixth Day Chinese United Press Dispatch)

Netherlands Participates in Anglo-Japanese Trade Conference

Japan Expresses Opposition to Dutch-Japanese Arbitration Treaty, Japanese Government Consults Privy Council

(Tokyo) On the sixth day, it was rumored that Britain, citing the existence of the Anglo-Dutch cotton industry agreement, intends to request Japan to recognize the Netherlands' participation in the Anglo-Japanese trade conference. However, the Japanese Foreign Ministry expressed its opposition to this claim for the following reasons: Although an agreement has been established between Britain and Japan, if Japanese goods are imported into Britain through the Netherlands, the purpose of the agreement cannot be achieved. Therefore, it advocates the participation of the Netherlands in the conference. However, the Japanese authorities' policy for the Anglo-Japanese and Japanese-Indian conferences is based on the principle of not discussing the market issues of third countries. If the British side proposes this issue, the Japanese government and people will definitely reject it. (Sixth Day Japanese United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Dutch-Japanese Arbitration Treaty was formally signed by Minister Saito and the Dutch Foreign Minister in The Hague on April 19th. The Foreign Ministry has received the full text of the treaty and will consult the Privy Council within days. Internal negotiations have begun. The purpose of this treaty is to resolve all issues between the Netherlands and Japan through mediation or arbitration and to promote friendly relations. However, recently, the Netherlands has been planning to form an economic group between itself and the Dutch East Indies, or to withdraw from various treaties that hinder import restrictions and tariff increases. Therefore, it previously declared its withdrawal from the tariff truce agreement and further expressed its intention to withdraw from the export and import restriction abolition agreement. Therefore, the trend of the Japanese-Dutch treaty at this time is particularly noteworthy. (Sixth Day Dentsu Dispatch)

(Moscow) This morning, a plane crashed near the Badulovsky North Lopasnia Station. Eight passengers died, including Baranoff, the Deputy Minister of Heavy Industry and Director of the Aviation Industry Bureau, and his wife, the Director of Civil Aviation, Goltzman, and his assistant, Zairzair, the director of Factory No. 22, Gorponov, and the plane's pilot and technician. (Fifth Day Reuters Dispatch)

He also said that he supports the British disarmament plan, but its details should be carefully studied. Dawes will stay in Britain for ten days before heading to France. (Sixth Day Havas Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Disarmament Conference was originally scheduled to be held in Geneva on October 10th. American Recovery Movement

President Asks Banks to Freely Extend Loans and Grant Grace Periods, Invites Ford to Join Industry Regulations

Havas, Chicago, Fifth Day -- President Roosevelt issued a letter to bankers, urging them to extend loans to industry and commerce as much as possible so that the National Economic Recovery Plan can succeed, saying, "The country needs courageous bankers, and there is no greater urgency than today."

Reuters, Washington, Sixth Day -- President Roosevelt asked the American Bankers Association to release credit loans so that industries can cope with the increased costs under its new industry regulations. This move has caused consternation. Association President Sisson claimed today that the authorities do not blame themselves for their failures but want to blame the banks. This kind of action only exposes their shortcomings and invites distrust.

Reuters, Washington, Fifth Day -- President Roosevelt met with members of the Recovery Administration today to discuss the domestic situation. It is expected that the authorities will give Ford, who has not yet accepted the automobile industry regulations, at least another 24-hour deadline to join the recovery movement.

Reuters, Detroit, Fifth Day -- It is now known that automobile magnate Ford has increased his daily minimum wage of four yuan by eight jiao.

Austria Increases Border Defense Strength

Rumors of the Current Prime Minister's Retirement

Reuters, Vienna, Fifth Day -- Seven aircraft flew to Innsbruck today to increase the strength of the troops on the Austrian-German border. Due to treaty restrictions, Austria cannot have military aircraft. The current aircraft are all privately owned, but the drivers are all police.

National, London, Sixth Day -- The Daily Telegraph's foreign affairs reporter predicted today that Austrian Prime Minister Dollfuss will resign soon. The doctor is very tired of the deepening opinions of the cabinet members and is exhausted from fighting against the growing National Socialist Party movement. Therefore, he decided to retire to make way for capable people. Moreover, the doctor deeply felt that if the people's trust in the government is not firm, then even if foreign financial and spiritual assistance is obtained, it would be useless. The newspaper also criticized the Austrian government's dispatch of several police aircraft to the German-Austrian border, saying that the Austrian government's excuse that the machines were privately rented in the hope of avoiding the crime of violating the treaty is, in fact, the crime of violating the treaty, which has become clearer.

Recognizes Boycotts as the Only Weapon Against Germany

Havas, Geneva, Sixth Day -- The World Jewish Congress held a meeting here last night. The Loss from the American and Cuban Windstorms is Extremely Heavy

Reuters, New York, Fifth Day -- The United States and Cuba have suffered severely from this storm. It is reported that more than 300 people have been affected near the Bay of Christo in Cuba. Along the coast of Texas, waves like mountains have arrived, covering a width of 200 miles, destroying wharves and houses along the water's edge. The tide has flooded the towns, and residents have fled by boat. The port of Rockport, thirty miles east of Corpus Christi, has suffered over one million gold dollars in property and ship losses. The business district of Corpus Christi has been flooded, and residents from News Bay to the Corpus Christi waterfront have fled. Reports of storm damage are still pouring in. It is also known that the town of Blancville is almost completely destroyed, and thousands of residents are homeless. The town is now at the center of a 50-square-mile flood. In the town of LeMontsville, only three houses remain intact, and there are many casualties in Harlingen. Troops have been requested to maintain order. The town of Sambini is also said to have been destroyed.

Reuters, New York, Sixth Day -- According to the latest survey of the storm on the coast of Texas, 32 people died and 1,500 were injured in Blancville alone, with material losses of several million dollars.

Norwegian Youth Invents New Type of Sound Receiver

Exceptionally Sensitive, the Fluttering of a Fly's Wings Can Be Clearly Heard

Reuters, Helsinki Correspondence -- A Norwegian young student, Larsen, invented a new type of sound receiver. With this, he can hear the conversation of two flies. It was recently tested at the Oslo University of Entomology in Norway. The instrument is very sensitive and can indicate the number of wing flaps when a fly flies. Even if it flaps its wings ten thousand times per second, it can be accurately noted. Larsen claims that he can use this instrument to listen to the sound of two insects rubbing their antennae or touching their sensory organs to talk. He hopes to solve the "insect language" problem soon and contribute to world scientists.

Song Ziwen Arrives in Lushan

Landed in Xun on the Fourth Day and Met with Jiang That Evening

Nanchang Correspondence: Finance Minister Song Ziwen, in response to Chairman Jiang's telegram, arrived in Lushan for a meeting. According to the Guling telephone obtained by the highest military and political organs and the report of the Xun Lake Garrison Headquarters, Minister Song, along with Deputy Finance Ministers Li Tiaoheng and Zou Lin, Secretary Huang Chundao, Director of the National Economic Council Qin Fen, and more than 30 guards, arrived in Xun on the Zhongshan warship at 11:30 AM on the fourth day. The warship was docked at the Ningshao pier. Chen, the garrison commander, Fang Rong, the captain of the Chu You warship, Bao Gongren, the county magistrate of Jiujiang, Zhou Xiangxian, the director of the Flood Prevention Committee, Yan Yan, the president of the Central Branch, and representatives from all walks of life in Jiujiang went to welcome them. The military police were heavily guarded. Song stood in the warship and waved his hat to the welcomers. He then accompanied Secretary Huang Chundao and his entourage ashore, took the Third Division Headquarters' No. 3 car to the 20th room of the Zhenxing Office Building for lunch. Jiang sent the director of the Xingying Liaison Office to take care of everything. When Chinese and foreign reporters stationed in Xun arrived, Song sent Secretary Huang to meet with them.
