Kung, Captain Lin Yuanquan of the Yingrui ship, Captain Gao Xianshen of the Ninghai ship, Staff Officer Ren Guanghai of the Training Fleet Headquarters, representative of Minister Chen Shaokuan, Deputy Director Chen Zaofan of the shipyard, Director Yu Zhenxing of the Pilot Training School, Battalion Commander Ye Baoqi of the Guard Battalion, Captain Zheng Yigong of the Minquan ship, Captain Yang Junsheng of the Desheng ship, as well as invitation personnel, Section Chief Liang Xunyu of the shipyard's Materials Department, Section Chief Ye Zaifu of the Shipbuilding Department, and Yu Jianfu, etc. In addition, shipyard inspectors Wang Zhiguang and Zeng Guocheng also attended.

The Grand Scene of the Bottle-Breaking

The shipyard specially prepared a small launch, the Victoria, at 1:15 PM to welcome guests at the new customs wharf. When they arrived at the shipyard, it was already 1 PM. The bottle-breaker was originally Mrs. Kung Hsiang-hsi (Soong Ai-ling), but Mrs. Kung was unable to attend due to an engagement and was replaced by her daughter, Miss Rosamond Kung. At 2:30 PM, all preparations were in place. Miss Kung held flowers in her left hand and the bottle in her right hand. After the electric bell rang, she aimed the bottle at the bow of the ship and threw it with force. With a loud crash, champagne splashed everywhere, and the ship slid into the Huangpu River amidst the cheers of the crowd. The Jiangnan tugboat towed it to the dock, and the ceremony was declared complete.

Refreshments

After the launching, all the guests took the small launch back to the shipyard dock and landed. They went to the auditorium for refreshments (however, Mr. T. L. Soong and Miss Kung had already returned to their residences). There were many guests, and they gathered together. Inspector General of Customs Mr. F. W. Maze and Section Chief Yu Jianfu of the shipyard went to another room and drank champagne together.

Shipyard Director's Speech

During the banquet, Deputy Director Chen Zaofan, representing Minister Chen Shaokuan, stood up and gave a speech, saying: "Today is the day of the launching of the Dexing Customs patrol ship, which was built by this shipyard. We are honored to have Mrs. Kung come to break the bottle, and we are also honored to have Inspector General of Customs Mr. Maze and gentlemen from all walks of life come to visit the ceremony. It is a great event, and we are very grateful. The Customs is not only the sole agency for the country to collect taxes, but also bears the important mission of investigating criminals, patrolling for bandits, and preventing smuggling. Now, Finance Minister Song, during this construction period, believes that the Customs' existing patrol ships are not sufficient for dispatch, and specially ordered the addition of many new patrol ships of various sizes. Because this shipyard is a national shipyard, it is highly trusted, and most of the new ships have been entrusted to this shipyard for construction. The Dexing patrol ship is one of the largest of these new ships. This shipyard has a long history of shipbuilding, and all its projects have always been praised by all sectors of society. In the future, we will continue to strive for excellence, so that all the new ships built for the Customs can assist the Customs, enhance its work, and increase its reputation, in order to live up to Minister Song's expectations. I also hope that all patriotic gentlemen in our country will follow Minister Song's trust in this shipyard and support and guide this shipyard. It is the good fortune of this shipyard and the glory of our country. Now that the autumn heat has not yet subsided, I dare not say more. I respectfully give this brief report and wish all the guests a long life for the Customs of the Republic of China and a long life for the Dexing patrol ship!" Then, Mr. Rickchard of the Customs gave a reply.

Overall Ship Structure

According to the person in charge of the shipyard, the Customs has built ten new patrol ships in this shipyard, and the Dexing ship is the first of these new ships. It is 170 feet long, 32 feet wide, 160 feet from the top of the mast to the bottom of the mast, 16 feet 6 inches deep, 11 feet 6 inches draft, 13 nautical miles per hour, and the displacement is 700 tons.

Workers at the Silk Factory Decide to Resume Work Today

The production quota system will be temporarily suspended.

Female workers at silk factories in Shanghai opposed to the implementation of the production quota system went on strike at 20 factories in the Zhabei Xinzha District, including Baotai. Through mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, it was decided that the production quota system would be temporarily suspended, and workers at all factories will resume work tomorrow morning. The details are as follows:

Continuing the Strike

Workers at twenty silk factories in the Zhabei Xinzha District on Changan Road, including Yuanxin Hongsheng, Xiexin, Baotai Fuxing, Chuxin, Maofeng, Hongchun Qianyuan Zhenxing Yuji, Jiyu Xieji, Hengfeng Road Meifeng, Yuanfeng Yonghe Road Jiyu Guangfu Road Wuxing, Jiatai Guangzhao Road Yuanxing Yuanji, and other factories, have been on strike since the 1st of this month, one after another, to oppose the implementation of the production quota system by the employers. The previous day, after the union advised them to resume work, the workers believed that there was still no solution, so they went on strike again after resuming work. Yesterday, the workers at each factory did not increase.

Yesterday's Mediation

Because the Social Affairs Bureau feared that the dispute would spread, it convened both parties for mediation at the bureau at 1 PM yesterday. Shen Huachen and Xu Peirong of the Silk Industry Association, Cui Ahui and Yang Shu of the Third District Silk Spinning Union, Yuan Yunlong and Yang Gengti of the Fourth District Union, and Chen Xiupu and Le Xiaoying of the Sixth District Union attended. Wang Xianqing, a staff member of the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, presided over the meeting, and Lu Yinchu, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, attended.

Resolution

First, the chairman inquired about the opinions of both parties, and then summarized the opinions of labor and management. The following resolutions were made: (1) The issue of the production quota system will be the responsibility of the Industry Association to notify all factories to temporarily suspend its implementation. (2) The Industry Association will formulate detailed measures for the production quota system and submit them to the Party and government organs for review and approval. (3) Tomorrow morning (i.e., today), the union will be responsible for advising all workers to return to work in the factory. At that time, both labor and management were satisfied and signed the agreement to resolve the dispute.

Temporary Suspension

The Social Affairs Bureau yesterday ordered the Silk Industry Association to comply. After investigating that various factories in the industry have reformed the wage system, the content and detailed measures of the production quota system have not been reported for review and approval in advance, and it was implemented on September 1st, which is inappropriate. In addition to ordering the union to advise workers to resume work on a specific date, it is hereby ordered to comply and quickly submit detailed measures for the production quota system for review and approval, and immediately instruct all factories to temporarily suspend its implementation. Do not violate this order.

Resumption of Work by a Specific Date

The Social Affairs Bureau yesterday ordered the Silk Spinning Industry Association of the Fourth and Sixth Districts to comply. After investigating that the Industry Association of the industry has rashly announced the implementation of the production quota system measures without approval, it is certainly inappropriate. However, the workers' hasty strike is also not justified. In addition to ordering the Industry Association of the industry to quickly submit detailed measures for the production quota system for review and approval, and immediately instruct all factories to temporarily suspend its implementation, it is hereby ordered to comply, and immediately instruct all workers to resume work by a specific date. Do not violate this order.

Union Notice

The Sixth District Silk Spinning Union issued a notice to all workers to resume work. The original text reads:

No Lockouts, Strikes, or Dismissals During Mediation and Arbitration

The Municipal Government Reaffirms the Prohibition

The New Voice News Agency reported that the Shanghai Municipal Government, in accordance with the provisions of the amended Labor Dispute Handling Law, stipulates that no lockouts or strikes shall occur during the mediation or arbitration period. Recently, employers at the British American Tobacco Company dismissed workers during the mediation period of the dispute, and the workers also went on strike, believing that it was contrary to government orders. Therefore, it issued a clear notice and reaffirmed the prohibition. The original notice reads: Shanghai Municipal Government Notice No. 103, regarding the notice, in accordance with Article 36 of the amended Labor Dispute Handling Law, employers or workers of each enterprise shall not suspend business or strike due to any labor dispute. Employers or workers of other industries or businesses whose disputes are in the mediation period or have been submitted to arbitration shall not suspend business or strike. Employers shall not dismiss workers during the mediation or arbitration period. The starting date of the mediation or arbitration period shall be calculated from the date on which the competent administrative agency notifies the parties to the dispute. Article 37 stipulates that workers or workers' organizations shall not engage in the following acts: 1. Closing shops or factories; 2. Taking or destroying goods or equipment of shops or factories without permission; 3. Forcing others to strike, etc. The restrictions on the actions of parties to labor disputes were announced by this government on July 5, 1929. Unexpectedly, recently, disputes have occurred between workers and employers, and there are still cases of going on strike or suspending business without following the legal procedures, or even destroying goods and equipment, as well as dismissing workers without authorization. This kind of behavior is both a violation of the law and a hindrance to order, and it is urgent to reaffirm the prohibition. In addition to ordering the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus, this notice is hereby re-issued for public information. If a dispute occurs between labor and management, you should immediately submit it to the competent authority for handling in accordance with the amended Labor Dispute Handling Law, and there shall be no violation of the restrictions on the above-mentioned actions. If anyone dares to violate this, this government will investigate and deal with it according to law without leniency. Sincerely, Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of the Republic of China, September 5, 1932.

Opening of the National Products Movement Exhibition Yesterday

Manufacturers decided to open on September 15th, discussed business rules and publicity plans.

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' United Association held a meeting of participating manufacturers' representatives at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on the third floor yesterday morning regarding the National Products Movement Exhibition. The signed factories included Juxin Enamel Factory, Samsung Thermos Factory, China Chemical Industry Society, Shuanglun Toothbrush Company, Xingye Weaving Factory, Jilu Needle Factory, Peacock Tie Company, Apuer Electric Appliance Factory, Shanghai Light Bulb Company, Huaguo Glass Factory Guanshengyuan, Wuzhou Factory, Huasheng Electrical Appliance Factory, and 167 others. Among the attending representatives were Yu Jiaxing, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Lixing, Wang Jingdong, Zhang Yichen, Liu Zhongying, Liang Genghua, and 276 others. At 11 o'clock, the meeting was opened with a bell, and Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, and Liu Zhongying were publicly elected as the presidium, with Zheng Dongshan as the recorder. After the ceremony, the chairman reported on the preparations, and then began the discussion. (1) Regarding the proposal to postpone the opening date, the chairman explained that the Public Works Bureau was deeply concerned about the building of reed sheds for the conference, fearing a recurrence of the enemy attack last year, so this year iron sheds must be used to avoid danger. However, iron sheds are expensive and time-consuming. In order to comply with the Public Works Bureau's proposal, the conference had to rebuild the iron sheds, so it must postpone the opening. Please vote to decide. It was decided to set the opening date as September 15th. (2) Regarding the proposal to draw lots for the site, it was decided to hold a lottery at 2 PM on Monday, September 10th (next week), still on the third floor of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. (3) Regarding the proposal to add discussion on business rules, it was passed item by item (original text omitted). (4) Regarding the discussion on the entertainment expenses proposal, it was decided to charge two cents per ticket, and the tickets will be distributed by the representatives of each factory. (5) Regarding the proposal to divide the Western currency area in the venue, it was decided that the conference will issue Western currency exchange coupons on a daily basis to show uniformity. (6) Regarding the proposal of whether to insure the goods in the venue, it was discussed that the conference should collect the prices of the goods from each factory and insure them with the insurance company. If the factory does not want to insure, it is also possible, and the expenses will be shared proportionally by the factories. Next, the publicity plan was passed. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM. The business rules and publicity plans are recorded as follows: (Temporary Business Rules for the National Products Movement Exhibition) (1) The venue will open at 8 AM every morning and close at 10 PM every evening. (2) The lights will be turned on at 6 PM every evening and turned off at 10 PM. (3) Participating factories are only allowed to sell their own products and shall not sell the products of other factories. (4) If participating factories sell non-national products or counterfeit national products that have been disguised, once discovered, all the goods will be confiscated, and the representative assembly will impose a fine. (5) Participating factories are not allowed to shout and sell in the venue. (6) The invoices of each factory will be formulated by the conference to show uniformity and avoid stamp duty (invoices will be obtained from the conference, 2 cents per book). (7) All participating personnel of each factory must wear a membership badge for identification (the badge will be obtained from the conference, 2 cents per badge). (8) If sizes and measures are required for the products sold in the venue, the Shanghai sizes and measures must be used. Others are not allowed to be used. (9) Participating factories shall not engage in irregular competition, such as giving one free with one purchase, or giving one foot with one foot purchase, etc. (10) The staff of each factory should treat customers peacefully and honestly, and should not deceive or quarrel with customers. If any of the above-mentioned incidents occur and damage the reputation of the entire conference, the conference has the right to order them to leave the conference. (Publicity Plan for the National Products Movement Exhibition) (1) Lantern parade (2) Car parade (3) Bicycle parade, scheduled to be held on September 20th (4) Hanging advertisements and slogans in public places (5) The conference will issue a large special edition of the venue daily, and a special edition of the exhibition (6) The conference will hold entertainment and film screenings every day.

Notice is hereby given that the factories in Xinzha District of this district have arbitrarily changed to the production quota system, which has caused dissatisfaction among the workers and a strike has been declared. This association has requested the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to handle it impartially. Yesterday, the Party and government organs convened both labor and management parties for formal mediation and have decided that the production quota system will not be implemented temporarily and that all workers will resume work from today. This notice is hereby issued for compliance.

Association Notice

The Silk Industry Association stated that the case has now been resolved by the Social Affairs Bureau, ordering both labor and management to resume work this morning. Xu Peirong and others were sent to notify each factory at 4:20 PM yesterday to start the machines at 5:45 AM today to await the workers' return to work. At the same time, the Industry Association stated that the production quota system has been ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau to be formulated in detail and submitted for review, so it was decided to convene a general meeting of representatives to discuss specific measures in order to submit them to the Party and government organs for approval.

A meeting was held the previous day, and due to time constraints, arbitration continued at 11:00 AM yesterday. Representatives from various departments of the New Factory Printing Section

However, some unethical individuals from our department, such as Pan Quanrong, Xu Wenqing, Chen Sihong, and Zhang Xiqi, were exploited by the factory to deceive and confuse workers, fabricate false information, coerce a return to work, and disrupt the work slowdown order, inciting universal public outrage. They even gathered a crowd of hooligans to disrupt the union, demonstrating extreme depravity and madness. This has caused our department's workers to be spat upon and cursed by all the workers, leaving an indelible stain on the labor movement. Fortunately, the union was able to maintain order, and their treacherous scheme was thwarted. Now, these driven dogs, Pan Quanrong and others, are again using the names of workers and issuing irresponsible announcements to slander the union, hoping to spread rumors and mislead the public. Upon hearing this, we feel deep indignation. Now, during this turbulent time for labor and management, our department's workers rely entirely on the union's leadership to seek liberation. We are determined not to associate with Pan Quanrong and others, and will not withdraw from the union and lose our safeguards. Besides firmly supporting the union, we hereby issue this statement."

To All

Regarding wages during the work slowdown, the old factory will provide 70% of the wages, and the new factory will provide 50%. The unresolved parts, such as the full payment of wages during the work slowdown at the new factory, and the reinstatement of worker number 938 at the new printing factory, are awaiting continued mediation by Party and government agencies. Their righteousness reached the skies. However, as the unrest was difficult to quell and there were many disputes, we have been too busy to express our gratitude individually. We hereby use these few words to express our sincere appreciation. We hope that you will take this into consideration. Respectfully, Shanghai Fifth District Cigarette Workers Union.

Yan Qingxiang Discusses Attending Three International Conferences

Central News Agency reports: Mr. Yan Qingxiang, the investor representative of China to the 17th International Labour Conference, was ordered to travel abroad in early April and has made great contributions at the conference. After the conference closed, he went to the Czech Republic, Denmark, Switzerland, Norway, and other countries to attend the World Cotton Conference and the World Power Conference. His tasks have now been completed. He arrived in Shanghai on the Conte Verde yesterday. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Yan yesterday to inquire about his trip, and he provided the following answers:

International Labour Conference

The International Labour Conference was held in Geneva from June 8th, with representatives from various countries participating. In addition to Yan Qingxiang, the Chinese delegation included Ji Yongxiang, the labor representative, and Xiao Jizhou, the government representative, as well as a Counselor of the Chinese Embassy in France. The conference opened on June 8th and did not close until the end of June. The conference period was very long, so there were many cases discussed. The proposals that were more closely related to China included: (1) the implementation of labor factory law; (2) equal treatment for foreign workers and local workers. These two proposals were put forward by China. The second proposal was also put forward by the Indian representative, but the results of the discussions were not passed, which was a pity. Because I still had to attend the World Power Conference, I left for Japan on the 24th without waiting for the case to close. All the conference affairs were left to the interim representative.

World Power Conference

The World Power Conference held its opening ceremony in Copenhagen, Denmark on June 26. Mr. Yan left Geneva on the 24th to rush to participate, and the day after the opening, he and representatives from various countries rushed to Kyoto, Switzerland to hold a formal meeting. On July 17, he went to the capital of Norway to hold the closing ceremony of the conference. Many cases were discussed at this conference. The general idea of each case was how to use natural forces to drive machines, such as the use of water power. In short, the conference was completely a technical conference.

World Cotton Conference

After the World Power Conference, Mr. Yan rushed to Prague, the capital of the Czech Republic, to attend the World Cotton Conference, as a representative of the National Yarn Industry Association. The conference period was short, and the cases discussed were all about various important issues related to the cotton yarn industry. One of the proposals was about the fraud that often occurs during the packing of American cotton, such as using inferior goods as silk goods, etc. How should such fraud be prevented in the future so that it can be eradicated? Mr. Yan continued by saying that after completing his official duties, he traveled to various places for inspection. All the documents are still en route because he returned to the country early. Once they arrive, he will sort them out and then go to Beijing to report on his mission.

A Shocking and Unheard-of Theft Case on the New Ning Shao Steamer

70,000 Yuan Escorted from the Ningbo Branch of the Kenye Bank to Shanghai, Only to Find Over 69,000 Yuan Stolen | A Five-Inch Square Hole Drilled in the Bottom of the Box

The Ningbo branch of the China Kenye Bank entrusted Wei Yuming, a steward of the New Ning Shao Steamer No. 22, with 70,000 yuan in banknotes packed in an iron box along with a passport from the Ministry of Finance, to be sent to Shanghai on the 5th of this month. However, when the steamer arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning, a five-inch square hole was discovered drilled in the bottom of the box, and 69,790 yuan of the stored banknotes had been stolen, leaving only over 200 yuan and the passport from the Ministry of Finance, etc. Shocked, steward Wei Yuming immediately reported to the Shanghai branch, which in turn reported to the Public Security Bureau, all police stations, and local police agencies, requesting a joint effort to investigate. The bank's legal advisor, lawyer Wu Linkun, also represented the bank in placing a reward advertisement, stating that anyone who can capture the perpetrators and recover the stolen goods, or provide information leading to the resolution of the case, will be rewarded with half of the recovered stolen goods. Last night, a reporter met with a senior official of the Kenye Bank, who said that whenever the Ningbo branch had funds to be sent to Shanghai, they were mostly entrusted to Wei Yuming, a steward of the New Ning Shao Steamer No. 22. This was because Wei's credit was outstanding and his family was quite wealthy. Moreover, his guarantor was also a prominent figure in the business community. Therefore, after the case occurred, there was no suspicion of Wei. The thieves in this case were exceptionally skilled. The theft of such a large sum of money was premeditated. When the steamer set sail from Ningbo, the thieves openly boarded the ship disguised as passengers. There were two of them in total. One of them was disguised as a servant and carried very simple luggage. After boarding the ship, the thief occupied a cabin alone and dressed and behaved in an extremely lavish manner. When the ship arrived in Shanghai, the two thieves leisurely tidied up their belongings and then went ashore. At that time, a steward on the ship was cleaning the cabins as usual. When he reached the iron box containing the banknotes, he suddenly found several things in the corner: iron chisels and scissors. While he was suspicious, he also picked up several pieces of iron. Upon closer inspection, they were the same color as the iron on the box. He quickly told Wei Yuming. When Wei rushed to check, he saw a hole in the bottom of the box. Upon inspecting the box, it was empty. There were many broken ropes used to tie the banknotes on the ground. The thieves had made the hole in the bottom of the box very small, and all the banknotes were in bundles of one thousand yuan, which were larger than the hole. Therefore, the thieves used scissors to cut the ropes tying the banknotes and slowly pulled them out one by one. At that time, Wei was almost out of his mind and reported to the comprador, and then urgently reported to the Shanghai branch. This is the whole story of the case. He added that the 70,000 yuan was the recent repayment of funds from Ningbo merchants. There were banknotes from the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks. Whether the case can be solved and the stolen goods recovered in the near future depends entirely on the efforts of the police.

An Interview with the Anti-Japanese Hero Jiang Minsheng

Unable to hold back tears when talking about his life experience | Polishing shoes while not forgetting to provide relief to the Northeast

Jiang Minsheng, an anti-Japanese hero and former major general, is struggling to make a living by relying on his own efforts. Since the failure of the anti-Japanese war in the Northeast, he feels ashamed of the people and the country. Since coming to Shanghai, he has humbled himself and taken on a lowly job, polishing shoes for people at the entrance of the Laidefang alley opposite the Cathay Theater on Avenue Joffre. The reporter, after hearing people talking about it, made a special visit to his workplace. Jiang Jun, who appeared to be about thirty years old, with a strong physique, was bending over polishing a person's leather shoes. His clothing was very untidy, and the shoes he was wearing were extremely worn. The reporter waited quietly for him to finish his work, then shook his hand and asked him questions. His speech was extremely passionate and intense. According to him, he felt heartbroken when he saw that the famous anti-Japanese heroes who came to Nanjing and Shanghai mostly lived in tall buildings, had plenty of food and clothing, and had many attendants. They traveled by car, sometimes to Moganshan, sometimes to Suzhou and Hangzhou, and their behavior was lavish. He himself had been fighting the Japanese invaders in Harbin for twenty years since the age of sixteen, and had now failed. He should have killed himself to apologize to the people, but then realized that as long as he lived for one day, he should fight for one day. The people of the Northeast are still waiting for us to return quickly and plan for a good opportunity to wait for another action. Therefore, he has endured the humiliation of doing this job to temporarily maintain his life. He participated in the major battles of Ma Zhanshan, Li Du, and Ding Chao. Although he has made some small contributions, it is difficult to compensate for the crime of losing territory. On April 26th last year, he was captured by the Japanese and released on May 14th. He came to Shanghai once, but did not dare to disturb all sectors and hurriedly returned to Jilin. He also participated in several major battles. The people of the Northeast still have great faith in the generals, with Wang Yizhe of the 67th Army, the volunteer army Wang Delin, Deng TieMei, and the former Jilin Chairman Cheng Yun being the most respected. In the future, he can cooperate with them to seek the restoration of lost territory, and only such people are qualified. When he came to Shanghai, he joined the Northeast Refugee Reception Center as a refugee from the Northeast. Fortunately, he was taken in, but he could not bear to sit and eat, so he personally took up this job. He has heard that foreign university professors and university students do not object to low-level occupations, so who is he to feel ashamed of it? However, recently his life has been severely bullied by imperialists, which is especially painful to his heart, because his workplace is often interfered with by patrolmen. After speaking, he couldn't help but shed tears, and the reporter also felt sad. It was also said that he had been repeatedly visited by philanthropists and industrialists, who asked him to go and live a better life, but he absolutely refused because he felt ashamed to accept it. At this point, a certain shoe factory sent shoe straps to meet Jiang Jun's professional needs. Jiang Jun repeatedly declined, and the sender left them anyway. 抗日英雄江民聲君（龔叔賢攝） "Anti-Japanese Hero Jiang Minsheng (Photo by Gong Shuxian)"

He had no choice but to temporarily accept them. It was said that Jiang Jun would sell them and donate the proceeds to the Refugee Relief Association. The reporter then asked about his daily income, which was about two or three yuan. The most common was 20 to 40 cents each time, and the most was one or two yuan. Jiang Jun, after deducting the minimum necessary for living, still sends all the money to the Northeast Refugee Relief Association. He currently lives in the refugee reception center at No. 25 Caishou Lane, Julida Road. His daily working hours are from 8:00 AM to 8:00 PM. Many people from all walks of life visit him. During the conversation, he often talked about his past and future in great detail.

Inheritance Dispute After Liu Xiji's Death

One Wife and Two Concubines Jointly Accuse the Eldest Son of Concealing Deeds in an Attempt to Embezzle the Estate

Liu Xiji, the general manager of the New World Company, passed away on June 10th of last year. During his lifetime, Liu first married Ms. Huang, who gave birth to a son named Miaosan, 23 years old, who currently resides at No. 82 Yongfeng Lane, North Sichuan Road. However, Ms. Huang died many years ago, and he then remarried Ms. Peng Yuezhen as his second wife. Later, he also took Ms. Xu Keqin and Ms. Qian Dingbao as concubines. Ms. Peng had no children. Ms. Xu gave birth to three sons and one daughter: Miaofang, 7 years old; Miaozhong, 3 years old; Miaofen, 2 years old; and Miaorong, 9 years old. Ms. Qian gave birth to two sons and one daughter: Miaoguang, 6 years old; Miaokun, 4 years old; and Miaoling, 7 years old. Liu Xiji also left a will before his death, dividing all his property into fifteen shares, with Peng Yuezhen and Liu Miaosan each receiving two shares. The remaining two concubines, five sons, and two daughters each received one share. One share was reserved for the public, and one share was specifically reserved for the future eldest grandson. Because his wives and children were mostly young, he entrusted his friend Li Minzhou to be the estate guardian and handed over all the estate to Li for management until the youngest child reached the age of 21. At that time, Liu Miaosan and others unanimously respected the deceased's wishes and followed the instructions. While handing over the property, they also recommended Liu Miaosan to entrust lawyer Yang Guoshu to submit a request to the First Special District District Court for the issuance of a certificate, allowing the guardian Li Minzhou to perform his custodial duties. While this was in progress, one wife and two concubines of Liu suddenly discovered that their husband had also purchased a piece of land in Yancang, Henan Province, Guangzhou, totaling 70 wells. Because they did not know where the ownership documents were stored, they still entrusted lawyer Yang to submit a request to the special court to temporarily postpone the announcement, and continued to investigate the whereabouts of the documents. They also invited Li Minzhou to hold a family meeting and decided to divide the land into four shares, with one wife, two concubines, and Liu's eldest son Miaosan each receiving one share. They then urged Miaosan to hand over the deeds he held, but Miaosan kept delaying. He originally lived with his stepmother, but because of this dispute, he moved to Yongfeng Lane on North Sichuan Road to avoid her, which further increased their animosity. Now, Peng Yuezhen, in conjunction with the two concubines, has hired lawyer Yang to file a lawsuit against Liu Miaosan, accusing him of concealing deeds in an attempt to embezzle the estate, requesting the court to expedite the case and order the defendant to hand over the deeds

The Engineering Department of the Economic Council Expedites the Formulation of Construction Plans for the Yellow River Disaster Area

Xi Dejiong Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning and Immediately Dispatched Personnel | Wu Shilin Reports on the Inspection of the Henan River Project

Mr. Xi Dejiong, Director of the Engineering Department of the National Economic Council, was recently summoned to Beijing by Chairman Song of the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee to plan construction projects in the disaster area downstream of the Yellow River. He returned to Shanghai yesterday morning. Mr. Wu Shilin, an engineer previously dispatched by the Council to inspect the flood situation in Henan and Luoyang, and the projects organized by the Henan Provincial Works Bureau, also returned to Shanghai yesterday. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Mr. Xi and Mr. Wu at the Engineering Department of the Economic Council yesterday to inquire about the river disaster and the inspection situation. The details are recorded as follows:

Mr. Xi's Remarks

According to Xi Dejiong, the report that he would take a plane to inspect the flood situation in the disaster area downstream of the Yellow River has been canceled. The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee has already received inspection reports from various provinces and water conservancy associations, and the situation is already clear. There is no need for him to go again, and there are many construction plans that need to be formulated urgently, so it is difficult to split himself. The zoning survey will be carried out by personnel dispatched by the Engineering Department, who will depart tomorrow or the day after. When Chairman Song of the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee went to Lushan, he entrusted Standing Committee Member Liu Ruiheng to preside over the meeting. Yesterday (i.e., the 5th) a Standing Committee meeting was held, and initial decisions were made on relief for various industries. After he returns to Shanghai, he will plan and draft a construction plan for the disaster area within a few days. After Chairman Song returns from Lushan, it can be reviewed and implemented.

Inspection Report

According to Wu Shilin, he was ordered to go to Henan from Hankou at the beginning of last month for inspection, and only returned to Shanghai yesterday after completing his duties. This year's Yellow River floods came very quickly. The water level in Mengjin and other places was highest on August 8th and 9th. Subsequently, due to multiple breaches in Lanfeng downstream and Hebei Province, the water flow accelerated, and the water level dropped by more than six meters in two days, and the riverbed was scoured to a depth of more than four meters. This water level and scouring situation were measured in Mengjin. The situation is similar in Kaifeng and other places. Therefore, in the current situation, the river channel has turned out to be better than before the flood. Because the riverbed has been scoured deeper and the water level has returned to the channel, the risk of horizontal overflow can be reduced. Although the levee at Zhuzui Ridge Ding Dam was damaged in Berniu Village, Guangwu Mausoleum, and Tiexie Town, and the water flow was forced into the south bank, there are fortunately 27 old dikes of various sizes for protection, so there is no immediate danger. Other places, such as Heijiang Estuary, have water seeping into the dike body, and the situation is very dangerous. With the careful protection of the Henan Provincial River Affairs Bureau and the Henan Provincial Works Bureau of our department, if the water does not rise again, it should not be in danger of breaking again. The Yellow River breaches this time were all caused by insufficient dike height. The water level along the river during this summer flood was almost the highest ever recorded in the same month in the past hundred years. The dike body was able to be preserved because the dikes were three or four feet to seven or eight feet above the water surface. The remaining people were spared from suffering another disaster. If there had been no dike construction work and this year's repairs, the overflow and collapse of the dikes along the river would have been even more harmful than in the Yellow River Basin. From this, we know that it is a matter of human effort, and it cannot be abandoned due to the difficulty of construction and lack of funds. and put Li Minzhou in charge as a guardian, so as to comply with the original intention of her late husband's will, etc." The First Special District Court opened a hearing, but because the defendant did not appear, it was postponed until yesterday morning for trial. However, the defendant still did not return from Shanghai and was unable to appear. Only the plaintiff's attorney appeared in court and made a statement. Judge Mo Runhua ordered a change of date for another hearing.

A Poor Private Tutor is Suddenly Assassinated

Nine Cuts All Over His Body, Intestines Flowing Out, Blood Gushing Like a Fountain | The Reason for the Murder is Said to Be Unlike a Revenge Killing, but Close to a Case of Adultery

At 0:30 AM yesterday morning, an assassination occurred in the jurisdiction of the Zhabei Fourth District Police Station, in the Sujia Lane area of ​​Tanjiaqiao. The victim was a poor private tutor. The following is a record of the investigation findings:

Impoverished Private Tutor

Chu Zhongfu, a native of Taixian, Jiangbei, was 39 years old. He was somewhat educated and had some knowledge of medicine. It is reported that he had married and had several children in his hometown. Some years ago, they suddenly had disagreements and separated. Chu came to Shanghai alone, but with nothing to his name, it was difficult to gain a foothold. Relying on his knowledge, he set up a fortune-telling stall at the empty space in Sujia Lane, Tanjiaqiao, at the end of Datong Road, relying on his silver tongue to tell fortunes for a group of superstitious people. Although it was not a bustling business, the income was enough to make a living. At the same time, the neighbors saw that Chu was composed and seemed to be a pitiful scholar in decline, so they encouraged Chu to set up a school to teach children. Chu was moved by this, and

Pitifully Poor

He borrowed a spare room from Qian Daoren (whose name is Yuqin), a native of Yancheng, who was over fifty years old, as a place to teach and live. There were also more than 20 children from poor families nearby who were eager to study. At the same time, Chu also treated people's illnesses and vaccinated children, so although he could not live a life of luxury for the past three years, he had no worries about food and clothing. Chu was also very friendly with Qian. It is reported that Chu had therefore worshiped Qian Yuqin as his teacher, and he was a vegetarian, worshiped Buddha, and chanted scriptures incessantly. However, his bed consisted of only two pieces of wood. Apart from that, he had nothing of value, yet he was still coveted by thieves. One night, while Chu was away, they stole it. Since then, Chu no longer prepared a bed. At night, he only used three long benches to make a temporary bed.

Sudden Tragic Death

The night before last (the 4th), Chu went out again and didn't return until 7 AM on the 5th. That same day, in the afternoon at 4 PM, he went out again and returned home at 8 PM in the evening, looking resentful. He immediately took a small stool and sat outside to cool off, not exchanging a single word with anyone. Shortly after, he went to bed. Who would have known that around 12:30 AM last night, Xiao, the 48-year-old wife of Qian Yuqin, was fast asleep when she suddenly heard loud barking outside. At the same time, there was also noise coming from where Chu was sleeping. Thinking that a thief had come again, Xiao hurriedly got dressed and went to check. She saw the door wide open and the dogs barking madly. She looked around but found nothing. When she turned back into the house, she saw that the door to Chu's bedroom was also open. She called out to him but got no response, so she hurried inside to check. She found Chu dead on his makeshift bed, with blood flowing freely and splattered all over the floor.

A Total of Nine Cuts

Xiao was greatly shocked by the sight and ran into her husband's bedroom, urgently waking Qian Yuqin. Together, they went out to investigate and saw Chu wearing a white undershirt and naked from the waist down, without pants. His intestines were also spilling out of his abdomen, making for a very gruesome scene. They quickly reported the incident to the Tan Jiaqiao Fourth District Police Station. Ge, the patrol chief of the station, and others went to investigate. At the same time, Xu Weijiang was dispatched by the Fourth District Headquarters to investigate. It was discovered that the deceased had been cut a total of nine times: three cuts to the head, one to the face, two to the left and right sides of the neck, one to the abdomen, one to the chest, and one to the right hand. The middle finger was severed, and the intestines were spilling out. Because the cuts to both sides of the neck were very deep, the head was almost severed. After learning of the circumstances of the death, the officers returned to the station to report. On one hand, they instructed the local bailiff to request an autopsy from the regional court. On the other hand, they summoned Qian Yuqin and his wife to the station for questioning.

Speculations on the Cause

According to Xiao's statement at the Fourth District Police Station, the deceased had been staying out overnight because he had a mistress. When asked how she knew, she hesitated and did not answer. At the same time, neighbors also reported to the police station that Xiao was highly suspected in this case. Therefore, the police station temporarily detained Xiao and ordered all subordinates to search for the murderer and bring them to justice. It was also learned that the deceased had an older brother and sister-in-law in his hometown, and neighbors had been notified to come to Shanghai to take care of the aftermath. As for the truth of the case, onlookers speculate that it was not a revenge killing but rather related to an affair.

Special Court in Tianjin for Shanghai Kidnappers

A total of nine kidnapping cases, seven in Shanghai and two in Tianjin

Jin Jiulin, the Inspector-General of the Special Agency of the First Detective Group of the French Police, along with Chief Detective Zhang Ziying, Deputy Detective Zhou Bingcheng, Detectives Cui Zhenduo, Qin Youyu, and others, previously arrested twelve men and women, including the major kidnappers Zheng Tangsheng, Shang Zhen, and Geng Huatang, in Tianjin and brought them to Shanghai. It was found that they had kidnapped Huang Yuyi, the deputy manager of the Zhongnan Bank; Chen Yanghe, the deputy manager of the Siming Bank; He Shaoting, the foreman of Xinsenji; Gu Zelin, the son of Yunnan division commander Gu Zizhen; Huang Baohua, and others in Shanghai. They also strangled Little Shaoxing on Avenue Petain and kidnapped Chen Zhuling and Liang Huiwu, the compradors of Jardine Matheson, in Tianjin, disposing of the bodies by burying them to eliminate the evidence. The details of the investigation and detention by the Second Special District Court have been reported in previous newspapers. During the investigation, the police also found that Cao Ziqing and Li Youren, two people who had been arrested and sentenced to imprisonment in the Public Concession, were related to the case and sent detectives to bring them to court and merge the cases for investigation. The investigation has now been completed. Yesterday afternoon, the court held a special session to formally begin the trial of this case. At 2 PM, the police sent the detectives in charge of the case to escort the defendants to court. The lawyers retained by the defendants, Wang Shizong, Hua Maosheng, Zhu Dianqing, E Sen, Zhan Jifeng, Jin Yu, and others, arrived at the court one after another to await instructions. When the bell rang three times, Judge Li Changnian, accompanied by Clerk Wang Baoxun, took the bench in the first courtroom to conduct the trial. The victims were not present. The bailiffs first brought the defendants to the court, and the judge asked for their names and ordered them to stand in order. After that, the police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stood up and presented the case, stating that the defendants were arrested by the police in Tianjin for kidnapping and brought to Shanghai, where they were detained and investigated by the court. It has been found that the first defendant, Zheng Tangsheng, the second defendant, Shang Zhen, the fifth defendant, Liu Yimin, the sixth defendant, Wu Shaoting, the tenth defendant, Geng Huatang, and the eleventh defendant, Li Yueshan, each committed crimes related to the kidnapping cases, either jointly or independently. There were a total of nine cases, two in Tianjin and seven in Shanghai. In the first case, on August 13, 1928, the police found a Liu surname hostage in a house at 755 Haig Road and arrested Li A'er, who confessed that Geng Tang instigated the kidnapping. Geng was not arrested at that time and was wanted. He has now been arrested. In the second case, on August 30, 1929, Liu Yimin and others kidnapped Chen Zhuling, the comprador of Jardine Matheson, in Tianjin and detained him at 4 Baokang Lane outside the Qiangzhe River in the British Concession. Chen committed suicide on the third day of his abduction, and his body was buried underground. In the third case, on May 27, 1930, at 6 PM, Huang Yuyi, the deputy manager of the Zhongnan Bank, who lived at 22 Baojian Road, was kidnapped on Haig Road. At that time, Huang's driver, Jiang Yunshan, and bodyguard, Wu Xueying, were killed, and another bodyguard, Ma Pinghan, was seriously injured. Afterwards, Wu Kunshan, who was sent by the victim to negotiate the ransom, was lured to Zhongshan Road and shot to death. Zheng Tangsheng and Shang Zhen were present at the scene. In the fourth case, on March 5, 1931, at 5 PM, Liang Huiwu, the comprador of Jardine Matheson, was kidnapped in Tianjin and hidden at 40 No. 38 Road in the British Concession. Three days after the kidnapping, his body was buried in the backyard garden. In the fifth case, on November 11, 1931, Shang Zhen was involved in the kidnapping of Chen Yanghe, the deputy manager of the Siming Bank, in front of 865 Avenue Foch. In the sixth case, on December 16, 1931, a person named Little Shaoxing had a feud with Fei Xinbao. Fei arranged for Liu Yimin and others to lure Little Shaoxing to Avenue Petain and kill him, abandoning the body and fleeing. In the seventh case, on January 6, 1932, at 10 AM, Gu Zizhen's five-year-old son, Gu Zelin, who lived at 95 Route Massenet, was kidnapped at the entrance of the West Adams Road West Adams Lane, with Zheng Tangsheng in charge of watching the hostage. In the eighth case, on August 30, 1932, the architect He Shaoting was kidnapped at 84 Bubbling Well Road, which was done by the same perpetrators in the sixth case. In the ninth case, on February 12 of this year, Huang Baohua was kidnapped in front of 25 Route Ghisi. The police are prosecuting Zheng, Shang, Liu, Wu, Geng, and Li under Article 1, Section 1 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Kidnappers and are requesting the court to investigate and deal with the matter according to the law. Fang Qingshan, Cao Ziqing, Li Youren, and others are highly suspected in the case, and the police still need to investigate them. Zheng Yinshi, Yu Yuanzhou, Chang Jianxi, Wang Shikong, Bian Zengyan, and others were initially detained on suspicion, but after investigation, they were found to be unrelated to the case, and the police are not prosecuting them and should ask the court to rule on the matter. The court verified the tickets and ordered the police to take the defendants down and examine them one by one. Zheng Tangsheng, Shang Zhen, Liu Yimin, Wu Shaoting, and others all confessed to colluding with other fugitives to commit the above cases and sharing the spoils. Geng Huatang confessed that the house at 755 Haig Road was rented on behalf of Chu Yupu's concubine and that he did not know about the kidnapping and did not know Li A'er, who was arrested in the case, and that he had no plans to kidnap someone surnamed Cai at 953 Avenue Joffre. Li Yueshan admitted to participating in the Gu Zelin and He Shaoting cases. Cao Ziqing and Li Youren also admitted to participating in the Liang Huiwu case. They are currently serving a 15-year sentence for another kidnapping case in the Public Concession. Fang Qingshan confessed that he was a cook at Geng Huatang's house and knew nothing about the kidnapping. Zheng Chenshi, Yu Yuanzhou, Chang Jianxi, Wang Shikong, Bian Zengyan, and others all confessed that they had no connection to the kidnapping case. By this time, it was dusk, and the judge ordered that the debate be adjourned to a later date. The defendants were returned to custody to await further instructions.

A Dead Thief's Body Found in Xiaobang River

Shot and Drowned in the River in the Dark; Autopsy Performed by the Court Yesterday and Body Claimed

Around 7 PM the night before last, four armed robbers, including Sun Qi from Qingkou, set out from Zhabei with the intention of robbing a resident at 180 Kunming Road. This was discovered by the Yulin Road Police Station. Chief Chinese Detective Su Changsheng, Yang Peisheng, Detectives Li Pengfei, Ma Wenda, and more than a dozen others, along with Western detectives, all armed, waited in ambush at strategic locations on Taopeng Road. After a while, Sun and the robbers arrived one after another. The detectives surrounded and apprehended them. In a panic, the robbers opened fire to resist arrest. The Chinese and Western detectives also drew their guns and returned fire. A total of more than twenty shots were exchanged. As a result, Sun Qi was captured on the spot, and the remaining robbers took the opportunity to escape. It was dark, so it was impossible to pursue them. A stray bullet injured an old woman, Shen Xu, and a young woman, Gong Baobao, both of whom were taken to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. Sun was taken to the police station, where he confessed that his accomplices were Xu Xiaoerzi, Wang Xiaoyubiao, and Kou Da, who had been invited to rob. The police chief ordered him to be detained. At dawn yesterday, a male corpse with a bullet wound in his abdomen was found in a small river on Taopeng Road. The police received the report and knew that it was Sun's accomplice. At the time of the attempted arrest, he was shot by the detective's return fire and fell into the river. They then took Sun to identify the body, which he confirmed was his accomplice, Xu Xiaoerzi. The detectives then took the body to the Fei Lun Road morgue to await the autopsy. Sun was escorted to the First Special District Court, briefly questioned, and ordered to be returned to custody. As for Xu's body, the prosecutor Guo Wei arrived at the morgue to confirm the cause of death. It was determined that the deceased, Xu Xiaoerzi, had resisted arrest and was shot in the abdomen by a detective on the spot, resulting in death. The body was handed over to Pushan Villa for burial.

Notorious Robber Yin Xinren Executed by Hanging

Requested Fruit Before Execution, Saying It Would Cleanse Him for His Heavenly Journey

Yin Xinren, a notorious robber from Taixing, 38 years old, was arrested for resisting arrest and shooting and killing Zhao Xiaohe, a detective, at a teahouse at 730 Avenue de France on October 22 of last year. He was escorted by detectives from the Laozha Police Station to the First Special District Court. In the waiting room, he boldly seized a handgun prepared by the Chinese police, hoping to commit violence and escape. He was apprehended, brought back to the police station, and interrogated. He then used bamboo chopsticks to stab a person delivering food to the prison, causing a wound of four to five inches. The injured person collapsed and was taken to the hospital for treatment by the police. The robber, who had committed numerous crimes, was eventually tried by the court and sentenced to death. The sentence was reported to the provincial government for approval. Yesterday morning, the day of execution arrived. The police escorted Yin to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The prisoner requested that the customary reward of wine and food, worth two yuan, be used to buy fruit, such as pears, bananas, and jujubes, for him to eat before his execution. He said that he would be a vegetarian before death, to cleanse himself for his heavenly journey, and that the remaining money should be used to buy paper ingots to be burned, so that he would have money to use in the underworld. After a while, the executioner, Judge Shen Shanzeng, arrived in court and ordered the prisoner to be brought to the court. He asked if he had any last words or wanted to send a letter to his family. Yin said that both of his parents were dead and his wife had gone with someone else, so he had nothing else to say. Judge Shen then ordered the Chinese and Western detectives to take Yin down, along with the entire case file and photographs, and escort him to the Caoxi Road execution ground in a car. The prosecutor appointed by the local court arrived at the scene to verify the identity of the person being executed. Yin Xinren was then hanged.

Shandong Compatriots Plead for Relief for the Great Yellow River Disaster

The Shandong Association in Shanghai Appeals to the National Government

Due to the Yellow River's flood, which caused disasters in Shandong, Henan, and other provinces, the Shandong Association in Shanghai telegraphed the Executive Yuan of the National Government the day before yesterday, saying: To Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, We humbly report that the Yellow River's flood has caused a major disaster in the four provinces of Shandong, Henan, Hebei, and Jiangsu, especially in the southwestern Shandong areas of Heze, Juye, Fanpu, Yuncheng, Dongping, and Shouzhang, where more than ten counties have been severely affected. The floodwaters have destroyed homes and drowned countless victims. Those who are fortunate enough to survive are suffering from the same plight and are in dire need of assistance. The situation is unprecedentedly tragic. As the Shandong Association is deeply connected to our homeland, we are deeply saddened and distressed. In addition to urgently raising relief funds for immediate assistance, we dare to appeal to the Executive Yuan to appoint senior officials to bring food and funds to provide immediate relief and save lives. Furthermore, the frequent disasters along the riverbanks of various provinces are primarily due to the lack of both funds and talent. We humbly request the Executive Yuan to allocate a portion of the cotton and wheat loan specifically for Yellow River management and to send the water conservancy experts hired in cooperation with the League of Nations to assist in the overall management of river control. In this way, the river can be secured, and the people can live in peace, which is the sincere hope and prayer of the Shandong people in Shanghai. We humbly request that our request be granted, and we await your orders with great trepidation. Shandong Association in Shanghai, respectfully.

The Shanghai Charity Federation Sent a Letter to Shanghai Charitable Organizations Yesterday, Seeking Donations for Yellow River Flood Relief

To the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Fundraising Association for Yellow River Flood Relief, We hereby inform you that the Shandong Association of Compatriots in Beijing sent a telegram stating that the Yellow River flood has caused a major disaster in the four provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, and Jiangsu. The southwestern Shandong areas of Heze, Juye, Fanpu, Yuncheng, Dongping, Shouzhang, and other ten counties have been particularly severely affected. The floodwaters have destroyed homes, and the victims are climbing trees, crying out for food. The elderly and weak are struggling in ditches and facing death. They are appealing to their relatives and friends for help and begging for food from door to door. Our association is deeply concerned about our homeland and is deeply saddened and distressed. We lack the means to provide relief and are extremely worried. We have always admired your association's commitment to providing assistance and helping the public. We hope that you will provide assistance and benefit the disaster victims. If you are willing to provide assistance and benefit the disaster victims, we hope that you will quickly raise a large amount of money for emergency relief so that the soup can save lives. The gratitude will be felt not only by our association. In anticipation, we send this telegram with our best regards. The Shanghai Charity Federation.

Report from the Special Commissioner of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee on the Yellow River Breach Disaster

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee considers the current Yellow River breach to be a major event and sent a special commissioner, Zheng Shouchang, to conduct an on-site investigation. The following is an excerpt from his report: I arrived in Xuzhou last month and reached Lanfeng by train on the night of the 1st of this month. The heavy rain had not stopped, and there were no hotels, so I went to the Chinese Anglican Church. With the guidance of Pastor Chen, I found that the water level had risen in the area on the 21st of last month, breaching the north-south embankment in the middle of the old Yellow River channel behind Zhenpu Village, about fifteen miles west of Lanfeng. The breach was about ten feet wide, and the water flowed eastward, covering an area up to three miles wide and reaching a depth of over thirty feet in Xuzhou. All the sandy land in the old Yellow River channel, planted with peanuts, crops, etc., was completely flooded. Later, I went to the mouth of the old Yellow River channel about half a mile outside the north gate. The water level had receded significantly, but it was still five or six feet deep. Although the water flowed eastward, it was still connected to the old channel. Unfortunately, the breached embankment has not yet been blocked. This is the situation of the flood in the area near Xuzhou and Lanfeng. Also, the area of Leizhai and Wuliji in the second and third districts, about thirty miles north of Lanfeng County, also breached at the same time, flowing eastward for a distance of sixty to seventy miles and spreading into Kaocheng County. From the south embankment to the north embankment to the border of Hebei Province, it is about a hundred miles long, and the water is more than ten feet deep (the water has receded, leaving yellow sand and soil), which is also about ten feet deep. The villages and fields along the embankment have been flooded, and countless people and livestock have died and been swept away. All that can be seen are treetops, houses, and land, all of which have been reduced to nothing. Those who escaped have no food or shelter. Wealthy families have either taken refuge with relatives or become beggars, while others live in makeshift sheds made of sorghum stalks, with only the clothes on their backs. Everything else has been lost to the flood. This is the tragic situation in the area north of Lanfeng.

Since its opening on the 21st of last month at 407 Jing'an Temple Road, the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Station has been providing prompt and courteous services for ticket sales, baggage handling, hotel reservations, and other services, which have been well received by all sectors. Promoting Chrysanthemum Cinerariifolium Planting for Home Industry

Chrysanthemum cinerariifolium has the effect of eliminating bedbugs, mosquitoes, lice, aphids, scarabs, all kinds of beetles, and pests on poultry, livestock, fur, and agricultural products, etc. Japan produces it annually, and besides its domestic use, its sales to China and Europe and the United States are more than 50 million yuan, an astonishing amount. The cultivation of this kind of agricultural product is harmless to rice and wheat, as it can be rotated after the autumn harvest every year. In rural areas, it can be an extra harvest in addition to rice and wheat. Now, the Family Industry Association is working directly with rural cooperatives in conjunction with the Shanghai Bank to provide seeds for planting. Experts are hired to guide the management and technology. All harvests will be purchased preferentially by the association. Although someone has organized this matter before, the scope was too small and the efficiency was minimal. Now that the Family Industry Association is promoting it, it is expected that the output in three to five years may exceed that of Japan, which is also good news for rural areas.
